Re: Dependency in profile in pom.xml  
Date  :-
Fri, 01 Aug 2014 04:08:06 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The ! at the beginning of the hadoop.profile property in hadoop-1.0 profile&#010;indicates that if the hadoop.profile property is not specified or absent,&#010;then the profile will be activated. So if you didn't specify it as a system&#010;property (e.g. -Dhadoop.profile=XXXX), it would be used by default.&#010;&#010;Given what I explained above, for your second question, you need to specify&#010;-Dhadoop.profile=2 and just omit -Phadoop-2 to activate the hadoop-2&#010;profile in your build.&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Deng&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Jul 31, 2014 at 7:29 PM, 李响 &lt;waterlx@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Dear maven user and developers,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Attached is pom.xml of Flume. I have some questions as follow, really&#010;&gt; appreciate your help or guide, thanks !!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1. Why profile id = hadoop-1.0 is the default profile ?&#010;&gt;     If not specifying -Pxxxxx for mvn command, I found hadoop-1.0 is the&#010;&gt; default one to use. why is it the default one ? is it&#010;&gt; because &lt;name&gt;!hadoop.profile&lt;/name&gt; is specified in its activation and&#010;&gt; hadoop.profile is not specified in properties ? Date  :-
Sat, 02 Aug 2014 13:19:07 GMT  
contents:- 
The Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Maven PMD Plugin, version 3.2&#010;&#010;A Maven plugin for the PMD toolkit, that produces a report on both code rule violations and&#010;detected copy and paste&#010;    fragments,&#010;    as well as being able to fail the build based on these metrics.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-pmd-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-pmd-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;3.2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Apache Maven PMD Plugin - Version 3.2&#010;&#010;Task&#010;* [MPMD-188] Require Java 6&#010;* [MPMD-182] Upgrade to PMD 5.1.2&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-
Sun, 03 Aug 2014 19:13:58 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven Assembly Plugin, version 2.4.1&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin&#010;&#010;The Assembly Plugin for Maven is primarily intended to allow users to aggregate&#010;the project output along with its dependencies, modules, site documentation,&#010;and other files into a single distributable archive.&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Assembly Plugin Version 2.4.1&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-637] - fileSet &lt;lineEnding&gt;unix&lt;/lineEnding&gt; strips last newline&#010;of file&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-651] - REOPEN - OutOfMemory when running maven-assembly-plugin&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-652] - Resource filtering does not work if line contains single @&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-696] - Internal Regexp Error with Windows Paths&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-639] - Change default for recompressZippedFIles back to true&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-682] - Make a link to the MavenArchiver documentation&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-686] - Update version of maven-filtering to 1.2&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-687] - Change the prefered location for assembly descriptors and filter files&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-690] - Think about WARNING for module dependencies&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-693] - Update XSD Versions in examples&#010; * [MASSEMBLY-694] - Generation of the site does not work with Maven 3.2.1&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

MD5 checksum validation tool [Windows]?  
Date  :-
Mon, 04 Aug 2014 16:16:05 GMT  
contents:- 
All the checksum validation tools I've found only seem to support files with format produced&#010;by the md5sum tool, ie -&#010;&#010;checksum1 relative/path/file1&#010;checksum2 relative/path/to/file2&#010;...&#010;&#010;But Maven publishes sibling files of the same name with ".md5" appended, and no relative path&#010;in the file. Does anyone know of a tool on Windows (shell extension, standalone GUI) that&#010;people could use after downloading the artifact (in this particular case it's an executable&#010;installer) and the md5 file and just double-click the md5 file to validate the download (or&#010;drag/drop the artifact and md5 file)?&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;This e-mail, including any attached files, may contain confidential and privileged information&#010;for the sole use of the intended recipient. contents:- 
Thanks, but the MD5 checksums file for the Tomcat installers have the filename in them (in&#010;the contents of the .md5 file, versus implied by the name of the .md5 file)&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;https://www.apache.org/dist/tomcat/tomcat-8/v8.0.9/bin/apache-tomcat-8.0.9.zip.md5&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;versus &#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;http://repo.maven.apache.org/maven2/org/eclipse/tycho/org.eclipse.tycho.embedder.shared/0.20.0/org.eclipse.tycho.embedder.shared-0.20.0.jar.md5&#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;The Tomcat md5 file is one that a tool like md5sum generates, and is the standard format that&#010;checksum validation tools expect. The tycho one is a standard maven-generated checksum file.&#010;It only contains the checksum, no path to the file because it's inferred by removing the ".md5",&#010;and consequently all these tools to validate the checksum don't work with the checksum files&#010;published in M2 repo. &#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#013;&#010;&gt; From: Mark Eggers [mailto:its_toasted@yahoo.com.INVALID]&#013;&#010;&gt; Sent: Monday, August 04, 2014 12:00 PM&#013;&#010;&gt; To: Maven Users List&#013;&#010;&gt; Subject: Re: MD5 checksum validation tool [Windows]?&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; -----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----&#013;&#010;&gt; Hash: SHA1&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; Justin,&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; This seems to work. Subject  :-
RE: Jococo report using Jenkins without the need to configure jacoco-maven-plugin? possible?  
Date  :-
Wed, 06 Aug 2014 14:31:37 GMT  
contents:- 
I believe you still need to configure jacoco-maven-plugin so that your tests are run with instrumentation,&#010;but you don't need to do the reporting part with maven. Jenkins will read the .exec file that&#010;Jacoco generates during test execution and publish reports from that. &#013;&#010;&#013;&#010;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#013;&#010;&gt; From: Dan Tran [mailto:dantran@gmail.com]&#013;&#010;&gt; Sent: Tuesday, August 05, 2014 9:31 PM&#013;&#010;&gt; To: Maven Users List&#013;&#010;&gt; Subject: Jococo report using Jenkins without the need to configure jacoco-&#013;&#010;&gt; maven-plugin? possible?&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; Hello,&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; I have an impression that I dont need bring in jacoco-maven-plugin to my&#013;&#010;&gt; poms, and just have Jenkins to run it at post build and magic will happen at&#013;&#010;&gt; Jenkins page.&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; So far, I have no luck with that&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; Any got this working?&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; Thanks&#013;&#010;&gt; &#013;&#010;&gt; -Dan&#013;&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;This e-mail, including any attached files, may contain confidential and privileged information&#010;for the sole use of the intended recipient. Short answer: no, that's not possible. contents:- 
I'm a new Maven user, using it almost completely through Eclipse.&#010;I've installed Nexus as a repository manager. It all works.&#010;&#010;1. Suppose I set up a dependency today, say on "needed-component". I&#010;have to explicitly reference the specific version I want, say&#010;"needed-component-2.3.4".  I had hoped there would be a way to just&#010;make a dependency to "needed-component" and have Maven keep me up to&#010;date with the latest version, but I gather that's not the Maven&#010;concept. Am I overlooking something?&#010;&#010;2. OK so I have the explicit dependency to "needed-component-2.3.4",&#010;set up using Properties-&gt;Maven-&gt;Add Dependency, finding the most&#010;recent version in central, etc.  Now is there any way to be notified&#010;via Nexus/Maven/Eclipse when a newer version of needed-component&#010;becomes available? Kind of a "check for component updates"?&#010;&#010;3. Failing that, I suppose I have to survey repositories like central&#010;myself and notice when new versions appear. OK so a year from now I&#010;see "needed-component-3.0.3" is in central. Is there any way via maven&#010;or maven/eclipse to update the original dependency, changing it from&#010;"needed-component-2.3.4" to "needed-component-2.3.4"?  Or do I have to&#010;go in and edit the dependency spec in the project's pom.xml file&#010;myself?&#010;&#010;4. Eclipse/Maven has an Add Dependency capability.  Suppose you make a&#010;conceptual or typing mistake when adding a dependency and want to&#010;revert.  Why no symmetric Delete Dependency? Again, is pom.xml editing&#010;the only recourse?&#010;&#010;Thanks for any help.&#010;&#010;- Les&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I had hoped there would be a way to just&#010;&gt; make a dependency to "needed-component" and have Maven keep me up to&#010;&gt; date with the latest version, but I gather that's not the Maven&#010;&gt; concept. Am I overlooking something?&#010;This gives you repeatable builds. If someone picks up your project and &#010;builds it, they will get a resulting artifact that is exactly the same &#010;one that you made.&#010;This is a good thing.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2. OK so I have the explicit dependency to "needed-component-2.3.4",&#010;&gt; set up using Properties-&gt;Maven-&gt;Add Dependency, finding the most&#010;&gt; recent version in central, etc.  Now is there any way to be notified&#010;&gt; via Nexus/Maven/Eclipse when a newer version of needed-component&#010;&gt; becomes available? Kind of a "check for component updates"?&#010;Usually you can subscribe to the forum or user group that is associated &#010;with that artifact.&#010;That way, you usually get a note about what new features are included &#010;and what old features have been changed or eliminated.&#010;Having new versions automatically adopted sounds pretty good until a new &#010;version breaks your build without you being aware that it was changed.&#010;You will tear your hair out trying to figure why your latest code change &#010;caused such a strange error in your application.&#010;It is a lot saner to try to have a stable set of dependencies from the &#010;start of a release cycle until the end.&#010;If you really need to upgrade a dependency in the midst of a development &#010;cycle, you want to do that as a separate task so that you can test the &#010;new version of the library with a stable version of your code.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3. Failing that, I suppose I have to survey repositories like central&#010;&gt; myself and notice when new versions appear. OK so a year from now I&#010;&gt; see "needed-component-3.0.3" is in central. Is there any way via maven&#010;&gt; or maven/eclipse to update the original dependency, changing it from&#010;&gt; "needed-component-2.3.4" to "needed-component-2.3.4"?  Or do I have to&#010;&gt; go in and edit the dependency spec in the project's pom.xml file&#010;&gt; myself?&#010;You should have a parent pom for your project and in that pom, you &#010;maintain the versions as variables. It has no code but you "install" it &#010;with Maven as a module.&#010;In your code modules, you specify the parent project by its GAV and you &#010;use the variables names for the versions in the GAV spec for a &#010;dependency org.apache.jackrabbit:jackrabbit-core:${jackrabbit.version}&#010;&#010;That way you only have to change one thing when you decide to adopt a &#010;new version of a dependency.&#010;Changing the variable jackrabbit.version in the parent will make sure &#010;that every module will be built with the same version of jackrabbit.&#010;&#010;You still need to rebuild each module but it will not require any &#010;editing of the module's pom.xml file.&#010;&gt; 4. Eclipse/Maven has an Add Dependency capability.  Suppose you make a&#010;&gt; conceptual or typing mistake when adding a dependency and want to&#010;&gt; revert.  Why no symmetric Delete Dependency? Again, is pom.xml editing&#010;&gt; the only recourse?&#010;&#010;Make sure that you are using Eclipse/STS or have plain eclipse with all &#010;of the m2e plugins that support Maven.&#010;If you do this, you have a very nice graphical editor for pom files and &#010;adding or deleting a dependency is just pointing and clicking and you &#010;will probably never use the "Add Dependency"&#010;It has a dependency navigation that makes it easy to see all of the &#010;transitive dependencies and you can also easily find all of the modules &#010;that require a version of one of the low level dependencies.&#010;(One click answers the question : "Who is dragging in version 1.0 of &#010;log4j?")&#010;&#010;STS from the Spring guys is a very good way to get Eclipse. It comes out &#010;of the box with all of the plug-ins required to use Maven.&#010;We started with plain Eclipse but every update was a really long process &#010;to find and load all of the plug-ins and it was hard to be sure that &#010;every team member had the same configuration of plug-ins.&#010;Once we found STS, Eclipse got a lot easier. One download and a single &#010;configuration to set up out SVN connection and the new version is ready &#010;to run. Takes 15-20 minutes to upgrade Eclipse now.&#010;&#010;&#010;Once you get your parent pom set up life gets pretty easy. Also look at &#010;dependency management.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks for any help.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Les&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Defining component by hint for plexus in pom.xml  
Date  :-
Fri, 08 Aug 2014 13:43:12 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;I'm trying to do some pretty advanced things with custom plugins with&#010;@Components.&#010;&#010;Basically, I want to use the same mojo with slight variations, and I want&#010;to be able to inject those variations via the pom (or via the &lt;packaging&gt;&#010;perhaps as well).  The plugin already defines a custom lifecycle, so I am&#010;ok if I have to define that lifecycle twice, I just don't want to have to&#010;define the 12+ mojos twice for almost the exact same thing.&#010;&#010;Essentially, I have a mojo that define a @Component:&#010;&#010;@Component&#010;Parser parser;&#010;&#010;&#010;I then I have two implementations of that Parser interface:&#010;&#010;@Component(role=Parser.class, hint="simple")&#010;public class SimpleParser implements Parser&#010;&#010;and&#010;&#010;@Component(role=Parser.class, hint="complex")&#010;public class ComplexParser implements Parser&#010;&#010;&#010;I know that on the mojo itself, could tell the mojo which one to use (by&#010;setting it like this: @Component(hint = "complex")&#010;&#010;but what I really want is to force the user to define the hint in the pom&#010;or command line.  But as far as I can tell, there is no way to do this.  Is&#010;there a way around this other than making two separate mojos, which then&#010;defeats the purpose of using plexus at all here as far as I can tell,&#010;because  I may as well just define the implementation explicitly (albeit,&#010;plexus would still be useful for test code, I suppose).&#010;&#010;Can I use an expression for the hint, and perhaps pass that as a separate&#010;parameter somehow?&#010;&#010;Any help or suggestions would be appreciated.&#010;&#010;-Ben&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ben Tatham&#010;Sr. Software Engineer&#010;Nanometrics Inc.&#010;+1 613-592-6776 x254&#010;http://www.nanometrics.ca&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Re: Defining component by hint for plexus in pom.xml  
Date  :-
Fri, 08 Aug 2014 14:13:25 GMT  
contents:- 
An easier way is to inject a Map of parsers keyed by the hint and then lookup the parser you&#010;require based on the configuration of the plugin.&#010;&#010;@Component&#010;private Map&lt;String,Parser&gt; parsers;&#010;&#010;@Parameter&#010;private String mode;&#010;&#010;Parser parser = parsers.get(mode);&#010;&#010;We currently have no way to make bindings from plugin configuration for injection. Something&#010;I'd like to do with the JSR330 work but not possible now.&#010;&#010;On Aug 8, 2014, at 6:43 AM, Ben Tatham &lt;bentatham@nanometrics.ca&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; I'm trying to do some pretty advanced things with custom plugins with&#010;&gt; @Components.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Basically, I want to use the same mojo with slight variations, and I want&#010;&gt; to be able to inject those variations via the pom (or via the &lt;packaging&gt;&#010;&gt; perhaps as well).  The plugin already defines a custom lifecycle, so I am&#010;&gt; ok if I have to define that lifecycle twice, I just don't want to have to&#010;&gt; define the 12+ mojos twice for almost the exact same thing.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Essentially, I have a mojo that define a @Component:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; @Component&#010;&gt; Parser parser;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I then I have two implementations of that Parser interface:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; @Component(role=Parser.class, hint="simple")&#010;&gt; public class SimpleParser implements Parser&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; and&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; @Component(role=Parser.class, hint="complex")&#010;&gt; public class ComplexParser implements Parser&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I know that on the mojo itself, could tell the mojo which one to use (by&#010;&gt; setting it like this: @Component(hint = "complex")&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; but what I really want is to force the user to define the hint in the pom&#010;&gt; or command line.  But as far as I can tell, there is no way to do this.  Is&#010;&gt; there a way around this other than making two separate mojos, which then&#010;&gt; defeats the purpose of using plexus at all here as far as I can tell,&#010;&gt; because  I may as well just define the implementation explicitly (albeit,&#010;&gt; plexus would still be useful for test code, I suppose).&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Can I use an expression for the hint, and perhaps pass that as a separate&#010;&gt; parameter somehow?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Any help or suggestions would be appreciated.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -Ben&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -- &#010;&gt; Ben Tatham&#010;&gt; Sr. Software Engineer&#010;&gt; Nanometrics Inc.&#010;&gt; +1 613-592-6776 x254&#010;&gt; http://www.nanometrics.ca&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Jason&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------&#010;Jason van Zyl&#010;Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&#010;In short, man creates for himself a new religion of a rational&#010;and technical order to justify his work and to be justified in it.&#010;&#010;  -- Jacques Ellul, The Technological Society&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
i think i got it,i debuged archetype:generate and found code like this&#010;&#010;DefaultFilesetArchetypeGenerator.java&#010;private File getOutputFile( String template, String directory, File &#010;outputDirectoryFile, boolean packaged,&#010;                                 String packageName, String &#010;moduleOffset, Context context )&#010;     {&#010;         String templateName = StringUtils.replaceOnce( template, &#010;directory, "" );&#010;&#010;         String outputFileName =&#010;             directory + "/" + ( packaged ? getPackageAsDirectory( &#010;packageName ) : "" ) + "/" + templateName.substring(&#010;                 moduleOffset.length() );&#010;&#010; Unlikely. The cost of the connection setup is negligible in the grand scheme of things if the&#010;connections are pooled and you're using something like SPDY/HTTP2 and a good client. Trying&#010;to manage TLS and non-TLS connections to the same server would not be worth the complexity&#010;for likely no performance improvement. Note that all Google servers are SPDY-enabled and all&#010;modern Android devices will connect using SPDY and this all scales and performs well.&#010;&#010;On Aug 13, 2014, at 7:25 AM, cody.a.fyler@wellsfargo.com wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Any chance we can use ssl only for the hashes and throw an error when validation fails?&#010;(as a future option)&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Cody Fyler&#010;&gt; Lending Grid Build Team&#010;&gt; G=Lending Grid Builds&#010;&gt; (515) – 441 - 0814&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#010;&gt; From: Hilton Wichwski Silva [mailto:hws689@gmail.com] &#010;&gt; Sent: Wednesday, August 13, 2014 9:19 AM&#010;&gt; To: Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Subject: Re: Testing Maven 3.2.3&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Example:&#010;&gt; http://blog.ontoillogical.com/blog/2014/07/28/how-to-take-over-any-java-developer/&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; 2014-08-13 11:16 GMT-03:00 &lt;cody.a.fyler@wellsfargo.com&gt;:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Just out of curiosity, why use https to download artifacts?&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; This does not seem like sensitive data that requires an encrypted &#010;&gt;&gt; connection.&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Cody Fyler&#010;&gt;&gt; Lending Grid Build Team&#010;&gt;&gt; G=Lending Grid Builds&#010;&gt;&gt; (515) - 441 - 0814&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#010;&gt;&gt; From: Jason van Zyl [mailto:jason@takari.io]&#010;&gt;&gt; Sent: Wednesday, August 13, 2014 12:36 AM&#010;&gt;&gt; To: Maven Users List&#010;&gt;&gt; Subject: Testing Maven 3.2.3&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; We have staged Maven 3.2.3 and I'd ask that users try and test this &#010;&gt;&gt; version because we have changed to using the HTTPS connection to Maven &#010;&gt;&gt; Central by default. Subject  :-
archetype:integration-test generated archetype build depends on parent project  
Date  :-
Wed, 13 Aug 2014 16:27:34 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;we use the archetype:integration-test to test if the archetypes we generate&#010;successfully compile.&#010;Our archetypes (we call them "quickstart") are located within the main&#010;project.&#010;So we have&#010;- parent&#010;  - core&#010;  - runtime&#010;  - clients&#010;  - quickstart&#010;     - quickstart-java&#010;     - quickstart-scala&#010;as a project hierarchy.&#010;&#010;To build the archetype generated by "quickstart-java" we need the artifacts&#010;from "core" and "runtime".&#010;So if we do a "mvn clean verify" on our project, and the user has not&#010;executed "mvn clean install" before (and the artifacts are not available&#010;online), the build fails.&#010;&#010;Is there a way to tell maven to add the artifacts from "core" and "runtime"&#010;into the tests classpath?&#010;Or can we somehow automatically execute the "install" phase when a user&#010;requests the "verify" phase?&#010;&#010;You can find our project here: https://github.com/apache/incubator-flink&#010;&#010;&#010;-- Robert&#010;&#010;

*Not answering your question* I think we have grown to favour moving away&#010;from APT and towards Markdown or Asciidoc as a format at least on the Maven&#010;team (note that we do not have good tooling for Asciidoc yet) most of our&#010;new documentation is driven through Markdown.&#010;&#010;I think there are really two plain text mark up formats left standing:&#010;Markdown and Asciidoc. Of those I think Asciidoc is the better format as it&#010;actually has a proper spec... but it could end up being the Betamax of&#010;formats (i.e. technically the best but looses out due to amount of Markdown&#010;usage out there)&#010;&#010;&#010;On 13 August 2014 18:22, Nick Burch &lt;nick@apache.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi All&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; For Apache Tika, we currently use the Maven Site plugin, along with the&#010;&gt; APT format for our site content. Name  :- 
Georgy Lago &lt;georgyl...@hotmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: AW: site-deploy using wagon-ssh: User input needed  
Date  :-
Thu, 14 Aug 2014 04:51:04 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi Gerrit,&#010;&#010;This is an old topic, and you may have solved it some way or another by now. &#010;But just as I struggled with this same problem, I figured I would share the&#010;answer for the benefit of others running into this.&#010;&#010;The problem is that 64-bit Windows has two system profile folders. 32-bit&#010;processes get redirected to %SystemRoot%\SysWOW64\config\systemprofile when&#010;accessing %SystemRoot%\System32\config\systemprofile.&#010;&#010;When you copied the .ssh\known_hosts file with Windows Explorer, you put it&#010;in the folder where only other 64-bit processes would see it.  You are&#010;likely running maven with a 32-bit Java and it is expecting to find the&#010;.ssh/ folder under the SysWOW64 system profile path.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Georgy&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/site-deploy-using-wagon-ssh-User-input-needed-tp5795624p5802252.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hello Georgy,&#010;&#010;thanks for your reply. I didn't expect any response to my problem after such a long time.&#010;So I was really surprised about your message. :)&#010;&#010;I have to admit that the system on which I tried it is a 64 Bit. And I placed the file into&#010;the System32 folder you mentioned. I'm not sure if there is a 32-bit Java, but it is possible.&#010;I will check this. Unfportunately at the moment I don't when I will have the time again for&#010;that. But as soon as I try it I will give you a response.&#010;&#010;Thank you very much for your message. :)&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Gerrit&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-----Ursprüngliche Nachricht-----&#010;Von: Georgy Lago [mailto:georgylago@hotmail.com] &#010;Gesendet: Donnerstag, 14. August 2014 06:51&#010;An: users@maven.apache.org&#010;Betreff: Re: AW: site-deploy using wagon-ssh: User input needed&#010;&#010;Hi Gerrit,&#010;&#010;This is an old topic, and you may have solved it some way or another by now. &#010;But just as I struggled with this same problem, I figured I would share the answer for the&#010;benefit of others running into this.&#010;&#010;The problem is that 64-bit Windows has two system profile folders. 32-bit processes get redirected&#010;to %SystemRoot%\SysWOW64\config\systemprofile when accessing %SystemRoot%\System32\config\systemprofile.&#010;&#010;When you copied the .ssh\known_hosts file with Windows Explorer, you put it in the folder&#010;where only other 64-bit processes would see it. Doxia Eclipse Editor Plugin problem with snippet macro  
Date  :-
Fri, 15 Aug 2014 01:06:50 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I have been successfully using the Doxia Eclipse Editor Plugin for a few &#010;months. But now I'm facing a compatibility problem related to the &#010;snippet macro. if I use the following macro:&#010;&#010;     %{snippet|file=${basedir}/src/path/to/file.txt}&#010;&#010;then the "mvn site" issues the error:&#010;&#010;     Error during retrieving content skip as ignoreDownloadError activated.&#010;&#010;If I remove the ${basedir} variable from the macro, the "mvn site" works &#010;as expected, but then I get this error in the eclipse IDE:&#010;&#010;     Doxia Converter Exception: &#010;C:\eclipse\install\dir\src\path\to\file.txt (path not found)&#010;&#010;I'm unable to specify the path of the snippet file in a compatible &#010;manner, I have tried using $basedir, ${basedir} and ${project.basedir}, &#010;but I always get the same results.&#010;&#010;Anyone has any suggestion?&#010;&#010;There are any plans to release an update of the Doxia Eclipse Editor &#010;Plugin which uses the same default directory as the "mvn site" command?&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;                 Pablo.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Re: Doxia Eclipse Editor Plugin problem with snippet macro  
Date  :-
Fri, 15 Aug 2014 14:26:48 GMT  
contents:- 
Ouch, bad news! This plugin has saved us hundreds of hours in APT format &#010;validation and also is a great memory saver. What are my alternatives &#010;for APT editing?&#010;&#010;Nevertheless, I've found a workaround for the problem I was facing, just &#010;in case someone else is experiencing it too:&#010;&#010;1.- Rename your APT file from file.apt to file.apt.vm, this seems to &#010;activate the preprocessor on maven.&#010;&#010;2.- Add this to the properties section of your pom file: &#010;&lt;basedir&gt;${basedir}&lt;/basedir&gt;&#010;&#010;3.- Use the snippet macro as follows: &#010;%{snippet|file=$basedir/src/path/to/file.txt}&#010;&#010;Now your macros are correctly recognized by maven and by the eclipse plugin!&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;                 Pablo.&#010;&#010;El 15/08/2014 14:30, Benson Margulies escribió:&#010;&gt; I made an official release once, I think, but since I no longer use&#010;&gt; Eclipse I am not in a position to maintain it further.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Fri, Aug 15, 2014 at 2:56 AM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Unfortunately, I dont think Doxia for Eclipse is maintained, and it never&#010;&gt;&gt; have an official release either&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; -D&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On Thu, Aug 14, 2014 at 6:06 PM, Pablo León &lt;pablo.leon@horus.es&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I have been successfully using the Doxia Eclipse Editor Plugin for a few&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; months. But now I'm facing a compatibility problem related to the snippet&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; macro. if I use the following macro:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;      %{snippet|file=${basedir}/src/path/to/file.txt}&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; then the "mvn site" issues the error:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;      Error during retrieving content skip as ignoreDownloadError activated.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; If I remove the ${basedir} variable from the macro, the "mvn site" works&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; as expected, but then I get this error in the eclipse IDE:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;      Doxia Converter Exception: C:\eclipse\install\dir\src\path\to\file.txt&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; (path not found)&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I'm unable to specify the path of the snippet file in a compatible manner,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I have tried using $basedir, ${basedir} and ${project.basedir}, but I&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; always get the same results.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Markdown is the way to go, there is a conversion as well [1]&#010;&#010;-D&#010;&#010;[1]&#010;http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/DISCUSS-Converting-site-documentation-to-Markdown-td5772521.html&#010;&#010;&#010;On Fri, Aug 15, 2014 at 7:26 AM, Pablo León &lt;pablo.leon@horus.es&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Ouch, bad news! This plugin has saved us hundreds of hours in APT format&#010;&gt; validation and also is a great memory saver. then the "mvn site" issues the error:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      Error during retrieving content skip as ignoreDownloadError&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; activated.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; contents:- 
notice this is referenced as DOXIA-373 [1] and used in DOXIATOOLS-15 [2]&#010;&#010;notice that you should:&#010;- avoid ${basedir} and prefer ${project.basedir}&#010;- not need the property in pom&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Hervé&#010;&#010;[1] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/DOXIA-373&#010;&#010;[2] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/DOXIATOOLS-15&#010;&#010;Le vendredi 15 août 2014 16:26:48 Pablo León a écrit :&#010;&gt; Ouch, bad news! This plugin has saved us hundreds of hours in APT format&#010;&gt; validation and also is a great memory saver. What are my alternatives&#010;&gt; for APT editing?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Nevertheless, I've found a workaround for the problem I was facing, just&#010;&gt; in case someone else is experiencing it too:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; 1.- Rename your APT file from file.apt to file.apt.vm, this seems to&#010;&gt; activate the preprocessor on maven.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; 2.- Add this to the properties section of your pom file:&#010;&gt; &lt;basedir&gt;${basedir}&lt;/basedir&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; 3.- Use the snippet macro as follows:&#010;&gt; %{snippet|file=$basedir/src/path/to/file.txt}&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Now your macros are correctly recognized by maven and by the eclipse plugin!&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;                  Pablo.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; El 15/08/2014 14:30, Benson Margulies escribió:&#010;&gt; &gt; I made an official release once, I think, but since I no longer use&#010;&gt; &gt; Eclipse I am not in a position to maintain it further.&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; On Fri, Aug 15, 2014 at 2:56 AM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Unfortunately, I dont think Doxia for Eclipse is maintained, and it never&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; have an official release either&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; &#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; -D&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; &#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; On Thu, Aug 14, 2014 at 6:06 PM, Pablo León &lt;pablo.leon@horus.es&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; I have been successfully using the Doxia Eclipse Editor Plugin for a few&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; months. &gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; then the "mvn site" issues the error:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;      Error during retrieving content skip as ignoreDownloadError&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;      activated.&#010;&gt; I have just confirmed Hervé is right, if you use ${project.basedir} then &#010;you don't need to add any property to your pom.&#010;&#010;El 17/08/2014 19:26, Hervé BOUTEMY escribió:&#010;&gt; notice this is referenced as DOXIA-373 [1] and used in DOXIATOOLS-15 [2]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; notice that you should:&#010;&gt; - avoid ${basedir} and prefer ${project.basedir}&#010;&gt; - not need the property in pom&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hervé&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [1] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/DOXIA-373&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [2] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/DOXIATOOLS-15&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Le vendredi 15 août 2014 16:26:48 Pablo León a écrit :&#010;&gt;&gt; Ouch, bad news! This plugin has saved us hundreds of hours in APT format&#010;&gt;&gt; validation and also is a great memory saver. What are my alternatives&#010;&gt;&gt; for APT editing?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Nevertheless, I've found a workaround for the problem I was facing, just&#010;&gt;&gt; in case someone else is experiencing it too:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 1.- Rename your APT file from file.apt to file.apt.vm, this seems to&#010;&gt;&gt; activate the preprocessor on maven.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 2.- Add this to the properties section of your pom file:&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;basedir&gt;${basedir}&lt;/basedir&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 3.- Use the snippet macro as follows:&#010;&gt;&gt; %{snippet|file=$basedir/src/path/to/file.txt}&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Now your macros are correctly recognized by maven and by the eclipse plugin!&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;                   Pablo.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; El 15/08/2014 14:30, Benson Margulies escribió:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I made an official release once, I think, but since I no longer use&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Eclipse I am not in a position to maintain it further.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Fri, Aug 15, 2014 at 2:56 AM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Unfortunately, I dont think Doxia for Eclipse is maintained, and it never&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; have an official release either&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; -D&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Thu, Aug 14, 2014 at 6:06 PM, Pablo León &lt;pablo.leon@horus.es&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I have been successfully using the Doxia Eclipse Editor Plugin for a&#010;few&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; months. But now I'm facing a compatibility problem related to the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; snippet&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; macro. if I use the following macro:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;       %{snippet|file=${basedir}/src/path/to/file.txt}&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; then the "mvn site" issues the error:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;       Error during retrieving content skip as ignoreDownloadError&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;       activated.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; If I remove the ${basedir} variable from the macro, the "mvn site" works&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; as expected, but then I get this error in the eclipse IDE:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Re: Remove old snapshots under local repository  
Date  :-
Mon, 18 Aug 2014 22:20:08 GMT  
contents:- 
I tend to use:&#010;&#010;     mvn dependency:purge-local-repository&#010;&#010;when sitting in a project directory, it'll go thru and delete all the &#010;SNAPSHOTs and re-resolve.&#010;&#010;The only problem with it in the default mode, is that is _only_ deletes &#010;the `.jar`. files and doesn't rebuild any metadata, so if you're using &#010;version ranges you're kinda f**ked.&#010;&#010;However, I usually use it with the following setting:&#010;&#010;     mvn dependency:purge-local-repository &#010;-DresolutionFuzziness=artifactId&#010;&#010;which will delete ALL files related to the artifact - all versions, all &#010;meta data - it doesn't mean there's more to download again but works &#010;wonderfully.&#010;&#010;MaRK&#010;&#010;On 18 Aug 2014, at 21:10, Adrien Rivard wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Or delete all directories that end with -SNAPSHOT&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Sun, Aug 17, 2014 at 8:18 AM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; sounds like a good option.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; xxx-1.0.0-20140816.071953-49.jar)?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; -D&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Easiest thing to do is to delete the entire organization or project&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;How do you generate a combined javadoc for a selection of submodules?&#010;&#010;I have added the javadoc plugin with the aggregate goal to the build as&#010;specified in&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-javadoc-plugin/examples/aggregate.html&#010;but it not generates javadocs for all submodules. Hi,&#010;&#010;At the moment, the aggregate javadoc report can only execute on the root of a &#010;multi-module build. This is partly a wanted feature to avoid too much javadoc &#010;generation and a workaround against problems with forked lifecycles: see &#010;MJAVADOC-171 [1]&#010;&#010;So this is simply not possible actually.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Hervé&#010;&#010;[1] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MJAVADOC-171&#010;&#010;Le dimanche 17 août 2014 03:51:43 robertmvn a écrit :&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; How do you generate a combined javadoc for a selection of submodules?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I have added the javadoc plugin with the aggregate goal to the build as&#010;&gt; specified in&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-javadoc-plugin/examples/aggregate.html&#010;&gt; but it not generates javadocs for all submodules. Hi,&#010;&#010;You can't specify this in the pom, but for now it would give you the  &#010;desired result.&#010;Since it's not possible with the current version of the javadoc-plugin,  &#010;other options which I can think of:&#010;- add a javadoc-profile or create a pom-javadoc.xml where you specify the  &#010;required modules.&#010;- reorganize the modules&#010;&#010;I understand that these are all suboptimal solutions, but maybe your rare  &#010;case needs something like this.&#010;&#010;thanks,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;&#010;Op Sun, 17 Aug 2014 21:27:37 +0200 schreef robertmvn &lt;forums@calitha.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; How would you specify this in a pom.xml ?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Robert Scholte-4 wrote&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Did you try it with the -pl (or --projects) argument?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Op Sun, 17 Aug 2014 20:13:43 +0200 schreef robertmvn &amp;lt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; forums@&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &amp;gt;:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; It's okay if the aggregate report only executes on the root of a&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; multi-module build. It's much easier to execute it as a separate action. In Jenkins-terms: a  &#010;post-build step, but I believe almost every CI server has an equivalent  &#010;solution.&#010;&#010;If you still want to solve this in the main pom.xml, you could do it with  &#010;the maven-invoker-plugin, though I wouldn't advice it.&#010;&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;Op Mon, 18 Aug 2014 18:02:24 +0200 schreef robertmvn &lt;forums@calitha.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; When talking about a CI solution, I assumed that the javadoc generation is  &#010;not required as part of the build-lifecycle, but could be executed as a  &#010;separate step.&#010;If that is a requirement, then a separate pom is not the preferred  &#010;solution, it'll make things much more complicated and you might be the  &#010;only one who understands it (once solved). Probably the clearest solution  &#010;is reordering your module structure, but I really wonder if it is worth it  &#010;just for javadoc...&#010;And of course there's the solution where you take the sources from the  &#010;plugin and add the feature yourself.&#010;&#010;I haven't had a look at dependencySourceIncludes/Excludes. Maybe JIRA[1]  &#010;has an answer. Search for "MDEP dependencySourceIncludes"&#010;&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;[1] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MDEP&#010;&#010;&#010;Op Mon, 18 Aug 2014 20:00:33 +0200 schreef robertmvn &lt;forums@calitha.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; The reason I ask about calling it from the main pom.xml is because I  &#010;&gt; don't&#010;&gt; quite understand how I can put all this in the maven lifecycle.&#010;&gt; If I would configure the javadoc plugin as in&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-javadoc-plugin/examples/aggregate.html&#010;&gt; in a separate pom-javadoc.xml and execute it as a separate action, then  &#010;&gt; it&#010;&gt; would process and compile those modules two times, right?&#010;&gt; So what I probably need is do the lifecycle in the main pom.xml, but  &#010;&gt; after&#010;&gt; the compile phase call a separate pom to generate only the javadoc.&#010;&gt; But I have no idea how to do this.&#010;&gt; Or maybe there is an easier way, but I don't see it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Another question is why the dependencySourceIncludes or&#010;&gt; dependencySourceExcludes isn't actually working.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Robert Scholte-4 wrote&#010;&gt;&gt; It's much easier to execute it as a separate action. In Jenkins-terms: a&#010;&gt;&gt; post-build step, but I believe almost every CI server has an equivalent&#010;&gt;&gt; solution.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; If you still want to solve this in the main pom.xml, you could do it  &#010;&gt;&gt; creating custom Maven resource filter  
Date  :-
Mon, 18 Aug 2014 15:02:50 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;We have projects with many property and xml files that need resource filtering per environment.&#010; &#010;&#010;For example in a property file one might see ${mysqlDbHost}, ${mysqlDbPw}, and ${mysqlDbUser}.&#010; There would also be a system variable called ENVIRONMENT.  Based on the ${propertyName}&#010;and ENVIRONMENT value, the resource filter would replace with the correct value.  This can&#010;be done with a DB (SELECT value FROM properties WHERE env="env" and name="propertyName") or&#010;via a web service (getPropertyValue?env=env&amp;name=propertyName).&#010;&#010;On the Maven side the solution seem to be to create a custom MavenResourcesFiltering.  The&#010;custom MavenResourcesFiltering implementation would do the lookups I mentioned above for each&#010;${propertyName} encountered in the resource files.&#010;&#010;1)  Is my assessment that creating a custom MavenResourcesFiltering is the way to go?  Maybe&#010;this problem is already solved already, since it does not seem unique?&#010;&#010;2)  I have visited multiple Maven articles on this but still have no idea how to implement&#010;it, the sites I visited are listed below.  Does anyone know of any document or can provide&#010;feedback on how to implement a custom MavenResourcesFiltering?&#010;&#010;It seems to me that at some point I would need a method that has either gets a list of all&#010;the ${propertyName}'s found in a file and the ability to provide the value for that property&#010;name.  Following the links I found I cannot tell where that method should be implemented&#010;and how to get it called from MyMojo.execute().&#010;&#010;1:  http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-filtering/&#010;2:  http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-filtering/usage.html&#010;3:  http://maven.apache.org/guides/plugin/guide-java-plugin-development.html&#010; &#010;Thank you!&#010;jose&#010;

Problem resolved.  The documentation in this link has the dependency tags in the wrong place... &#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-resources-plugin/examples/custom-resource-filters.html#Dependency_declaration&#010; &#010;When I moved the plugin's dependencies tag outside of the configuration tags then everything&#010;worked.  Who ever manages that link please investigate.  Everything else on the site was&#010;spot on.&#010; &#010;thanks&#010;jose&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tuesday, a system variable called ENVIRONMENT.  Based on the ${propertyName} and&#010;ENVIRONMENT value, the resource filter would replace with the correct value.  This can be&#010;done with a DB (SELECT value FROM properties WHERE env="env" and name="propertyName") or via&#010;a web service (getPropertyValue?env=env&amp;name=propertyName).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On the Maven side the solution seem to be to create a custom MavenResourcesFiltering. &#010;The custom MavenResourcesFiltering implementation would do the lookups I mentioned above for&#010;each ${propertyName} encountered in the resource files.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1)  Is my assessment that creating a custom MavenResourcesFiltering is the way to go? &#010;Maybe this problem is already solved already, since it does not seem unique?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2)  I have visited multiple Maven articles on this but still have no idea how to implement&#010;it, the sites I visited are listed below.  Does anyone know of any document or can provide&#010;feedback on how to implement a custom MavenResourcesFiltering?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; It seems to me that at some point I would need a method that has either gets a list of&#010;all the ${propertyName}'s found in a&#010; file and the ability to provide the value for that property name.  Following the links I&#010;found I cannot tell where that method should be implemented and how to get it called from&#010;MyMojo.execute().&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1:  http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-filtering/&#010;&gt; 2:  http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-filtering/usage.html&#010;&gt; 3:  http://maven.apache.org/guides/plugin/guide-java-plugin-development.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you!&#010;&gt; jose&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Am I missing something here?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks&#010;&gt; jose&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Monday, August 18, 2014 3:08 PM, Jose Martinez  &#010;&gt; &lt;jmartx@yahoo.com.INVALID&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Karl,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you for responding.  Yes I can go into more detail.  &#010;&gt; Lets go back to my example of the mysql DB credentials.  Lets say I have  &#010;&gt; five environments.  So that means I have 3 variables times 5  &#010;&gt; environments and that comes out to 15&#010;&gt;  various values.  From what I understand about the  &#010;&gt; maven-resources-plugin that would mean I would have to do one of the  &#010;&gt; following:&#010;&gt; 1)  Stick those 15 values in the pom and then maybe use 5 different  &#010;&gt; profiles, one for each env.  This can get quite cumbersome and our  &#010;&gt; deployment scripts&#010; would have to call mvn with the correct profile.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2)   Use system variables.  Have some code called at some point before  &#010;&gt; the maven build that would know which environment it is in and retrieve  &#010;&gt; all the values for each known property and make system variables out of  &#010;&gt; them.  From what I understand this might still require I have them in  &#010;&gt; the POM; I'm not sure if maven-resources-plugin would automatically  &#010;&gt; replace each ${propertyName} with the proertyName system variable  &#010;&gt; without having to have the propertyName in the POM?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010; 3) Is there another way that I am missing that this can be done using  &#010;&gt; maven-resources-plugin?  I can see that it is very powerful tool, as  &#010;&gt; everything in Maven has proven to me to be so I'm probably missing  &#010;&gt; another approach.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A few things to consider that I would like to have...&#010;&gt; 1) Centralized view into all our properties that can be queried and have  &#010;&gt; tools built on top of (e.g. a maven resource filter).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) Minimal entries of propertyName.  Essentially the ${propertyName}  &#010;&gt; should only be entered into the property file and after&#010; that just the  &#010;&gt; entries that go into the central data store.  The pom is left alone.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3) Environments can be easily added and removed and altered by only  &#010;&gt; touching the centralized datastore.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I guess those three&#010;&gt;  things have one thing in common, benefits of having our properties in a  &#010;&gt; centralized datastore.  At my current employer they built just such a  &#010;&gt; system that works off of web services (managed global properties on a  &#010;&gt; per environment basis).  It is not in production yet so from my point of  &#010;&gt; view I will interface out the Dao and just swap implementations when its  &#010;&gt; ready... using a simple relational DB at first.&#010;&gt; thanks&#010;&gt; jose&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Monday, August 18, 2014 2:06 PM, Karl Heinz Marbaise  &#010;&gt; &lt;khmarbaise@gmx.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hi Jose,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ${mysqlDbPw}, and ${mysqlDbUser}.  There would also be a system  &#010;&gt;&gt; variable called ENVIRONMENT.  Based on the ${propertyName} and  &#010;&gt;&gt; ENVIRONMENT value, the resource filter would replace with the correct  &#010;&gt;&gt; value.  This can be done with a DB (SELECT value FROM properties WHERE  &#010;&gt;&gt; env="env" and name="propertyName") or via a web service  &#010;&gt;&gt; (getPropertyValue?env=env&amp;name=propertyName).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ${propertyName} encountered in the resource files.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 1)  Is my assessment that creating a custom MavenResourcesFiltering is  &#010;&gt;&gt; the way to go?  Maybe this problem is already solved already, since it  &#010;&gt;&gt;
